## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (ordinary differential rate laws)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is an instantaneous concentration rate of change, with features time t and concentration A, which is the standard setup for kinetic rate laws and their time-dependent or concentration-dependent variants (e.g., reaction order, reversible approach to equilibrium, autocatalysis). With only (t, A), the most common models express dA_dt as a function of A alone (autonomous kinetics) or as A multiplied by a time-varying rate constant k(t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order decay/formation: dA_dt = c0 (constant-rate production or depletion, e.g., surface-limited regimes)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, pseudo-first-order conditions)
- Nth-order rate law: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (elementary/empirical reaction order; includes second-order when c1 = 2)
- First-order with background source/sink: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A (net of constant feed plus linear loss, or linearized kinetics near a point)
- Reversible first-order relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to A = c1 with timescale 1/c0)
- Quadratic (Riccati) kinetics: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (captures competing pathways, recombination, or truncated mechanistic expansions)
- Autocatalytic/logistic-type kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth with depletion/limiting capacity)
- Bimolecular with limiting reactant lumped into constant: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (c1 - A) (A reacting with B where total B is c1 and B = c1 - A)
- Time-varying pseudo-first-order rate constant (linear drift): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (changing temperature/catalyst level over time, slowly varying k(t))
- Time-varying pseudo-first-order rate constant (exponential drift): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (accelerating/decaying effective rate constant over time)
- Driven kinetics with periodic modulation: dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (periodic forcing such as light intensity or feed oscillations)
- Inhibition-like rational rate (empirical): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (effective slowing at high A due to self-inhibition or limited active sites)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt depends only on A (no explicit t), expect an autonomous rate law; trajectories A(t) shift in time but keep the same dA_dt vs A curve.
- Approximately linear dA_dt vs A indicates first-order (or linearized) kinetics; the slope gives an effective rate constant and the intercept indicates a source/offset.
- A stable nonzero steady state occurs when dA_dt contains a factor (A - c1) or a root at A = c1; sign change around that root implies relaxation to equilibrium.
- Strong curvature in dA_dt vs A (concave/convex) suggests higher-than-first-order terms (A**2, A**c1) or competing pathways (quadratic polynomial in A).
- Autocatalysis is suggested when dA_dt is near zero at A ≈ 0 but becomes positive for intermediate A (presence of an A factor multiplying a positive term).
- If apparent rate changes systematically with time at fixed A, model k(t) explicitly via (c0 + c1*t) or c0*exp(c1*t), multiplied by A for pseudo-first-order behavior.
- Oscillatory forcing or external modulation appears as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) factors multiplying a baseline rate, often as (1 + amplitude * sin(...)) to keep sign structure.
- A bounded concentration range (approach to a maximum or depletion to zero with slowing near an endpoint) often corresponds to factored forms like A*(c1 - A) or (A - c1).

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (CRK18)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_p*sin(c3*A)
Candidate formulas: 51

GT is the fixed function of \(A\) (no \(t\)-dependence):
\[
f(A)= -0.5637231318832533\,A^2 + 0.1313786441969526\,\sin(0.7616913890711074\,A).
\]
So any matching candidate must be reducible (by choosing its free constants) to “quadratic in \(A\) + single sine in \(A\) with zero phase shift + no extra terms”, and must be independent of \(t\).

---

### 1. \(A c0 + A c1 + A^{c2}c3 + c4\sin(Ac5+c6)+c7\)
Can set linear terms to 0 (choose \(c0=-c1\) and/or both 0), set \(A^{c2}c3\) to \(-0.5637A^2\) by \(c2=2, c3=-0.5637\). Sine can match frequency/amplitude by \(c4=0.1313786, c5=0.7616914\). But phase: need \(c6=0\) (mod \(2\pi\)). Constant offset \(c7=0\). This *can* match.  
**However** note there are two separate linear terms \(Ac0+Ac1\); easiest set both 0. Works.

### 2. \(A c0 + A^{c1}c2 + c3\sin(Ac4+c5)+c6\)
Set \(c0=0\). Set \(c1=2, c2=-0.5637231318832533\). Set sine \(c3=0.1313786441969526, c4=0.7616913890711074, c5=0\) (mod \(2\pi\)). Set \(c6=0\). No \(t\).  
**Matches GT.**

### 3. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + c2 + c3e^{c4 t} + c5\log(c6e^{Ac7}+1)\)
To remove \(t\): need \(c3=0\) (or \(c4=0\) but then constant remains; still removable by setting \(c3=0\)). Remove log term: \(c5=0\). Then left with \(A^2c0+Ac1+c2\), cannot produce sine term.  
**No match.**

### 4. \(A^2c0 + A^2c1 + Ac2 + Ac3 + c4 + c5\cos(c6\log(c7e^{Ac8}+1))\)
Can collapse quadratics to one coefficient, kill linear terms, kill cosine term by \(c5=0\), but then no sine. If keep cosine term, it’s not \(\sin(kA)\) (argument is \(\log(1+\alpha e^{\beta A})\), not linear in \(A\)).  
**No match.**

### 5. \(A^2c0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3)\)
This has exactly quadratic + sine. Choose \(c0=-0.5637231318832533\), \(c1=0.1313786441969526\), \(c2=0.7616913890711074\), \(c3=0\) (mod \(2\pi\)).  
**Matches GT.**

### 6. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + A^{c2}c3/(A^{c2}+c4) + c5\cos(c6\log(c7e^{Ac8}+1))\)
To match GT must remove extra non-GT terms: set \(c1=0\), set rational term to 0 by \(c3=0\), set cosine term to 0 by \(c5=0\). Then only \(A^2c0\) remains, missing sine.  
**No match.**

### 7. \(Ac0+Ac1+Ac2 t + c3 + c4\sin(Ac5+c6)+c7\log(c8e^{Ac9}+1)\)
Must remove \(t\): \(c2=0\). Remove log: \(c7=0\). Then only linear-in-\(A\) plus sine plus constant; cannot create \(A^2\) term.  
**No match.**

### 8. \(A^2c0 + A^{c1}c2 e^{c3 t} + c4\sin(Ac5+c6)+c7\)
Remove \(t\): set \(c2=0\) (or \(c3=0\) but then term remains as power). If \(c2=0\), lose ability to add anything useful; still can match with \(A^2c0 +\) sine + constant by setting \(c7=0\). Yes: choose \(c0=-0.5637\), \(c4=0.1313786\), \(c5=0.7616914\), \(c6=0\), \(c7=0\), and \(c2=0\).  
**Matches GT.**

### 9. \(A^2c0 + A c1 (c2+t)^{c3} + c4\sin(Ac5+c6)+c7\)
To remove \(t\): need \(c1=0\). Then becomes \(A^2c0 +\) sine + constant; set \(c7=0\) and match coefficients as before.  
**Matches GT.**

### 10. \(A^2c0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3)+c4 + c5\exp(c6\cos(c7\log(c8 t^2+1)))\)
Remove \(t\)-dependent exponential term: set \(c5=0\). Then \(A^2c0 +\) sine \(+c4\). Set \(c4=0\) and match.  
**Matches GT.**

### 11. \(A^2c0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3)+c4\)
Set \(c4=0\) and match quadratic and sine as in #5.  
**Matches GT.**

### 12. \(A^2c0 + A^2c1 + c2\sin(Ac3+c4)+c5\)
Combine \(A^2\) coefficients: choose \(c0+c1=-0.5637231318832533\). Set sine \(c2=0.1313786441969526\), \(c3=0.7616913890711074\), \(c4=0\). Set \(c5=0\).  
**Matches GT.**

### 13. \(A^2c0 + Ac1+Ac2+Ac3 + c4\sin(Ac5+c6)+c7\)
Kill linear terms by setting \(c1=c2=c3=0\). Set \(c7=0\). Match \(c0,c4,c5,c6\) to GT.  
**Matches GT.**

### 14. \(A^2c0 + Ac1+Ac2 + c3 + c4\cos(c5\log(c6e^{Ac7}+1))\)
If kill cosine term \(c4=0\), left with quadratic+linear+constant, no sine. If keep cosine, wrong functional form.  
**No match.**

### 15. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + c2\cos(c3\log(c4e^{Ac5}+1)) + c6 e^{Ac7}\)
Hard to remove non-GT terms: can set \(c2=0\) and \(c6=0\), then only quadratic+linear remains (no sine).  
**No match.**

### 16. \(A^2c0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3)+c4 + c5 t^{c6}\log(A^2c7+1)\)

**Matches GT.**

### 17. \(A^2c0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3)+c4 + c5 t\)

**Matches GT.**

### 32. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + c2\cos(c3\log(c4e^{Ac5}+1)) + c6\log(c7e^{Ac8}+1)\)

### 34. \(A^2c0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3)+c4 + c5 e^{Ac6}\sin(Ac7+c8+c9 t)\)

### 35. \(A^2c0/(Ac1+c2) + Ac3/(Ac1+c2)+Ac4/(Ac1+c2)+ c5\sin(Ac6+c7)\)
Rational terms in \(A\) cannot simplify to a pure polynomial \(-0.5637A^2\) for all \(A\) unless degenerate (but denominator would have to be constant and still gives at most \(A^2\) scaled? If \(c1=0\), denominator \(=c2\) constant, then first term becomes \((c0/c2)A^2\) good; but then the other two become linear terms \((c3/c2)A\) and \((c4/c2)A\) which can be zeroed by \(c3=c4=0\). Then we have quadratic + sine, and can match sine with \(c5,c6,c7\) (phase \(c7=0\)). Works.)
**Matches GT** (choose \(c1=0\), \(c2=1\), \(c0=-0.5637\), \(c3=c4=0\), \(c5=0.1313786\), \(c6=0.7616914\), \(c7=0\)).

### 36. \(Ac0 + c1 + c2(|Ac3|+1)^2 + c4\sin(c5\log(c6e^{c7|A|}+1)+c8)\)
Has \((|A|+1)^2\) structure giving \(A^2\) plus unavoidable constant and linear-in-\(|A|\) pieces unless \(c2=0\) (then lose quadratic). Sine argument is log-exp in \(|A|\), not linear in \(A\).  
**No match.**

### 37. \(A^2c0 + A c1/(Ac2+c3) + c4\sin(Ac5+c6) + c7/(Ac2+c3)+c8\)

### 38. \(A^2c0 + Ac1 + A c2 e^{c3 t} + c4 + c5\log(c6e^{Ac7}+1)\)

**No match.**

### 39. \(A^2c0 + A^{c1}c2 + c3\sin(Ac4+c5)+c6\)
Set \(c2=0\) to remove extra power term (or could try to fold into quadratic but then would duplicate quadratic unless set \(c0=0\); still possible). Easiest: \(c2=0\). Then quadratic+sine+constant; set \(c6=0\) and match.  
**Matches GT.**

### 40. \(A^2c0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3)+ c4 e^{Ac5}+c6\)

**Matches GT.**

### 41. \(A^2c0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3)+ c4\log(Ac5+1)+c6\)

### 42. \(A^2c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t} + c3\sin(Ac4+c5) + c6 e^{c2 t}+c7\)

### 43. \(A^2c0 + A c1 e^{Ac2} + c3\sin(Ac4+c5)+c6\)

### 44. \(A^2c0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3)+ c4\log(Ac5/(A+c6)+1)+c7\)

### 45. \(A^2c0 + A c1 e^{c2 t}/(A+c3) + c4\sin(Ac5+c6)+c7\)
